  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c4a8b8a-3778-4770-8223-01624ca39a52'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1760389790170584663">Second book in Starbirth series. <br/><br/>Lock Harford, a teleporter (Shifter) who moves through another dimension using the power of thought, works alongside British Special Forces in trouble spots around the world. His employers at the British Secret Intelligence Service (MI6) need him to eliminate lethal weapons that will bring world war—and ultimately world destruction. Terrori</span>
  <span id="freeText1760389790170584663" style="display:none">Second book in Starbirth series. <br /><br />Lock Harford, a teleporter (Shifter) who moves through another dimension using the power of thought, works alongside British Special Forces in trouble spots around the world. His employers at the British Secret Intelligence Service (MI6) need him to eliminate lethal weapons that will bring world war—and ultimately world destruction. Terrorists are using the new weapons to inflict heavy losses on British Special Forces in the conflict zones of Afghanistan and the borderlands by Iran. <br /><br />Taking Special Air Service troopers with him, including his colleague Jimmy Mackenzie and his team, Lock is embroiled in fierce battle. The situation is precarious when personal enemies, bent on eliminating Lock and Jimmy before they can find the weapons, pursue them across the world. <br /><br />This is a powerful tale of terrorism in a dangerous world where new human powers are commonplace and growing. Intertwined with the action are elements of humanity and humour that make these books accessible to everybody, embroiling the reader in the lives and conflicts of the characters.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reg Shell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reg Shell" href="/user/show/32409409-reg-shell">Reg Shell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376981967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1391446156728533584">This book was a step outside my usual comfort zone of reading as I’ve not read many works of this nature. J.M.Johnson’s The Shifter Dimension 3 is categorized as Science Fiction> Genetic Engineering, Fantasy > Paranormal & Urban. It is all those and was a great introduction into that detailed realm.<br/><br/>I began this series with book three and I was able to follow the story. I will be picking up and reading books 1 and 2. It’s an interesting story.</span>
  <span id="freeText1391446156728533584" style="display:none">This book was a step outside my usual comfort zone of reading as I’ve not read many works of this nature. J.M.Johnson’s The Shifter Dimension 3 is categorized as Science Fiction&gt; Genetic Engineering, Fantasy &gt; Paranormal &amp; Urban. It is all those and was a great introduction into that detailed realm.<br /><br />I began this series with book three and I was able to follow the story. I will be picking up and reading books 1 and 2. It’s an interesting story.</span>

  <span id="freeText1818558058943657973" style="display:none">Having read the first in the Starbirth series, which I loved I was looking forward to reading this book. I was not disappointed.<br /><br />Although, I found the beginning a bit slower this time, I enjoyed the read nevertheless. The dialogue was well thought out and written. The military aspect felt very genuine.<br /><br />If you like military scifi you may want to consider reading this.</span>

<div id="review_2737517017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2737517017" />
    <a title="Jeanette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11029945-jeanette"><img alt="Jeanette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442988435p2/11029945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2737517017?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette" href="/user/show/11029945-jeanette">Jeanette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35024851-the-shifter-dimension">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2737517017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2449676732211227902"><i>The Shifter Dimension</i> by J. M. Johnson is the second book in the Starbirth trilogy. It picks up where the first book <i>Starbirth Assignment</i> left off. <br/><br/>Lock Harford (teleporter) and his family are under threat by Maria Zamora (transmute) who wrongly blames him for killing her boyfriend. He fights the restrictions of the SAS and Ministry of Defence would impose on him, but eventually rejoins SAS soldier Jimmy (James Mackenzie) and the D-squadron in Afghanistan to fight terrorists who can both shift (</span>
  <span id="freeText2449676732211227902" style="display:none"><i>The Shifter Dimension</i> by J. M. Johnson is the second book in the Starbirth trilogy. It picks up where the first book <i>Starbirth Assignment</i> left off. <br /><br />Lock Harford (teleporter) and his family are under threat by Maria Zamora (transmute) who wrongly blames him for killing her boyfriend. He fights the restrictions of the SAS and Ministry of Defence would impose on him, but eventually rejoins SAS soldier Jimmy (James Mackenzie) and the D-squadron in Afghanistan to fight terrorists who can both shift (teleport) and have access to powerful weapons of mass destruction. <br /><br /><i>The Shifter Dimension</i> is a well-written book with high-octane action and a strong hold on military and intelligence operations in the theatre of war. It explores the murky world of espionage and some of the outcomes and issues raised by the sudden rise of people with psychic superpowers. <br /><br />While Harford features strongly in this story, the threat posed by Maria was largely tangential to the story and it felt in many ways more like Jimmy's story. While it includes a romantic subplot (mostly from Jimmy's point of view), the majority of the characters are male (as in the first novel). With the title, I was hoping for a greater exploration of the nature of the 'shifter dimension' (there are a few additional hints and perhaps that will become clearer in the third book). A few passages felt more like reportage (with lots of indirect speech), but they were few and far between and overall, the book held my interest and kept me engaged in the action and the characters. <br /><br />A solid second book with the promise of more to come. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2449676732211227902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14397806942123907702">I judge a book on its ability to hold my attention and keep me hooked until the very end. The Shifter Dimension did this for me. I had never read this type of book before so at first I found the world of Shifters intriguing and as I read on I became absorbed in the credible alternate world Jackie Johnson had created. Lock Harford, is forced back onto active duty to protect his family. Working with the Secret Service and British Special Forces he sets out to track down terrorists who have a new d</span>
  <span id="freeText14397806942123907702" style="display:none">I judge a book on its ability to hold my attention and keep me hooked until the very end. The Shifter Dimension did this for me. I had never read this type of book before so at first I found the world of Shifters intriguing and as I read on I became absorbed in the credible alternate world Jackie Johnson had created. Lock Harford, is forced back onto active duty to protect his family. Working with the Secret Service and British Special Forces he sets out to track down terrorists who have a new deadly weapon. As Lock utilizes his special talents what follows is a different type of pacy thriller with lots of twists and turns as the mystery/adventure unfolds. The read is made all the more satisfying with the addition of a number of well rounded characters, goodies and baddies. An enjoyable read and highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14397806942123907702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2184287817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2184287817" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9912834-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571534226p2/9912834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2184287817?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/9912834-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35024851-the-shifter-dimension">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=cliffhanger-laden">cliffhanger-laden</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=military-sf">military-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=r-rated">r-rated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9912834-caitlin?shelf=self-published">self-published</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184287817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11095119277714964915"><strong>A paranormal military thriller. </strong><br/><br/>It's a bit hard for me to classify this book, as it's not in a genre I've read much in; I think the closest descriptor would be military science fiction, but of the near-future variety rather than military space opera. Lock Harford is a Shifter (i.e., teleporter) with other psychic powers including aura detection. He makes use of these abilities to lead a Special Forces team dedicated to protecting Britain from threats at home and abroad, which means sometimes goi</span>
  <span id="freeText11095119277714964915" style="display:none"><strong>A paranormal military thriller. </strong><br /><br />It's a bit hard for me to classify this book, as it's not in a genre I've read much in; I think the closest descriptor would be military science fiction, but of the near-future variety rather than military space opera. Lock Harford is a Shifter (i.e., teleporter) with other psychic powers including aura detection. He makes use of these abilities to lead a Special Forces team dedicated to protecting Britain from threats at home and abroad, which means sometimes going against the will of his handler, Stephen Stringer. <br /><br />I liked the paranormal angle in this book. It was a bit reminiscent of the X-Files and helped set the book apart from a standard military thriller. That said, Johnson clearly knows her stuff in that department, and the seemingly realistic use of military lingo and terminology provides verisimilitude without devolving into impenetrable MilSpeak. The recap of what happened in Book 1 is also skillfully done, such that even though this was the first book in the series I read, I quickly got up to speed. <br /><br />However, I did have some issues with the pacing, especially in the first third of the book before the team sets off for Afghanistan. There were a few too many instances where conversations between characters were summarized when I would have liked to see the dialogue written out. A couple characters like Spooky Nick and Bilton also drop out of the picture without much explanation. The characters in general aren't super-strong in this book; they're mostly crafted to play various roles, which is fine, but as a character-driven reader I could have done with a bit more. <br /><br />All in all, this was a pretty good military SF read; I had fun with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11095119277714964915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2281358827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281358827" />
    <a title="Judith Rook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42082104-judith-rook"><img alt="Judith Rook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462537945p2/42082104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281358827?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith Rook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith Rook" href="/user/show/42082104-judith-rook">Judith Rook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781535485449" href="/book/show/37656357-the-shifter-dimension-starbirth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281358827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8542543211152176590">Projection for the Future<br/><br/>‘The Shifter Dimension’ by J M Johnson, Book 2 in the ‘Starbirth’ series, is one of the better novels in a somewhat over-populated genre. It is very well written by an author who creates a completely authentic, realistic setting and who has a considerable flair for description, which cannot be said for many writers of action books.<br/>The storyline is very successful and is bound to interest readers of military and secret service operations, especially those who enjoy techno</span>
  <span id="freeText8542543211152176590" style="display:none">Projection for the Future<br /><br />‘The Shifter Dimension’ by J M Johnson, Book 2 in the ‘Starbirth’ series, is one of the better novels in a somewhat over-populated genre. It is very well written by an author who creates a completely authentic, realistic setting and who has a considerable flair for description, which cannot be said for many writers of action books.<br />The storyline is very successful and is bound to interest readers of military and secret service operations, especially those who enjoy technological details. There are many details of technology, both already existing and those which come from the author’s speculative imagination and provide the slight world-building content of the book.<br />In some instances, the narrative falls into the trap of over-explanation. There is perhaps too much description; the details of the teleportation process, for example, while fascinating at first appearance, are somewhat overdrawn when continued throughout the book.<br />There is excellent development of some characters, but others tend to be flat and almost stock-character in nature. Perhaps the reason is that such a complex and extremely well-controlled storyline takes over from the full presentation of human action and motivation.<br />‘The Shifter Dimension’ is a substantial novel, containing a great deal of direct narration, which sometimes becomes a little ponderous. This is probably necessary, because the book is part of a series, and the back story and forward projection are built into its structure.<br />However, it is a technically accomplished, very readable book, well worth the purchase price and highly recommended.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8542543211152176590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3Gn7OGC3uOL/3sa9OlA5honqqvDucT3/Sby9MMgVsB9k7qoKAQ2sfpKsEJvGLv0RutU23HKuGc5tbZCzZpWpog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ybHbEfjKzZUXvWspG9+pNWnZj8Ts27qiZySNDZVOTpRxNoojmXDZCXrPvQ/noW2iWuYT6HAEnpND9aCOO85XKQ==')})
  }

And they were all true. I\'d come back from distant shores and speak of my adventures. That’s all.  But although I’m known mostly as a raconteur - and most of my books can be described as coming from the humourist vein – in ‘Nobody Asked Me’ I touch on some subjects that are surely going to upset a few people.  I’ve never quite understood the politically correct brigade. Hardly any subject is taboo to the Englishman when he’s laughing. No longer simply a fad, blogging is now an important new literary innovation. This book is not a story, and if you’re looking for a book that is all sweetness and light, please give this one a miss. It’s not for you. I won’t be offended and I honestly wish you a great life. If everyone likes me, then I’m not being controversial enough – and trust me when I say that in this book I get controversial.  Oh, don’t worry; the humour that my fans seem to enjoy so much is still there, but right now the planet’s spinning in new and scary directions, and this needs to be addressed. So inside the covers of this book I take a look at some of the challenges we’re currently facing. And some of my opinions are going to rattle a few people.  So is a comedy writer honestly the best one to challenge some of the perceptions we’re facing nowadays? Well, I’ve always believed that if you can make people laugh then they tend to listen to what you say when you’re serious. And my goal, my life’s ambition if you like, is to give direction to comedy, purpose to satire.  So why the rabbit popping out of a tin of soup on the cover. Well ‘Rabbit &amp; Pork’ is Cockney rhyming slang for Talk, and on more than one occasion I’ve been accused of rabbiting away excessively – mostly at parties, and generally by my wife.  But why a tin of soup? Well I tend to believe that everyone is born perfect. Nobody is born with an inherent capacity to hate. It has to be taught. All of our experiences – family, school, work, the books we read, the newspapers we peruse, the music we listen to, our friends, our social life, the opinions of those around us, religion, sports we play or watch, those we love and those who love us, those we desire and those who desire us, those we travel with, our hopes and dreams and ambitions and achievements, our triumphs and disasters - go into a metaphorical cooking pot that we carry with us throughout our lives.  All these ‘ingredients’ make up our Soup of Life.  Now, when making a soup, once you’ve added an ingredient, it’s forever blended in and you can’t take it out again. You add a sprinkling of finely chopped garnish; cumin or oregano, and you can never take that ingredient out again. Never, ever, ever. So say at the age of six you add black pepper or rosemary or hatred or love or comedy, from then onwards it’ll always be part and parcel of your ‘soup.’ And as you add more ingredients the ‘recipe’ of your life evolves, and before you know it you can’t taste the coriander or the love any more, but it’s still there at a deep subliminal level. Remember that. <script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_50846763'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50846763-anxiety?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Anxiety<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17514757.Danny_Winter?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Danny Winter<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.35 avg rating &mdash; 17 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published \n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer2283269805371540818\">This book of prose and magnificent poetry is Danny’s story as he begins to notice the world around him start to shatter. Yet through all that he offers encouragement and inspiration to those millions of others who also experience anxiety and panic.\n\n<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2283269805371540818\" style=\"display:none\">This book of prose and magnificent poetry is Danny’s story as he begins to notice the world around him start to shatter. Yet through all that he offers encouragement and inspiration to those millions of others who also experience anxiety and panic.\n\nThere are many books on the market about anxiety, yet just a quick glance at these will demonstrate just how chintzy, patronising and condescending they really are. All these books give the impression that a few simple exercises can hold the terrors of tension, misery and dread at bay. If only it was that easy. But it’s not. Anxiety can cripple you! And there’s no easy cure, or magic words, or wrist band that is ever going to work \n\nWe start the book as Danny takes stock of those around him, and as editor of the book, before we get into more serious matters, I’ve allowed Danny 15 quick-fire poems to introduce himself, his Gypsy lifestyle as a kid and where he finds himself at the moment. He begins to notice loss, although he never phrases it quite like that. But we see loss as children fly the nest, loss of his youthful good looks and energy, a possible loss of income and finally the loss of a friend of ours, Chalkie, who was brutally murdered.\n\nOur mate, Chalkie, was a great friend to Danny, and when he was savagely murdered it sent Danny into dark places in his mind that he had trouble escaping from. Danny was very much aware that he was in danger of turning corners in the labyrinth of his mind that he may not be able to find his way out of.\n\nDanny has become a student of the human condition, and in this book he does what he does best; write poems about the world around him, and he does this with passion. Even if poems aren’t your preferred treasure, even if they don’t normally grab you, if they’re not your ‘thing,’ I’d still ask that you bear with Danny as he tells his story in his own way, for this, some would say, is what happens when someone with anxiety digs deep down into his own soul, for the book looks into the nitty-gritty of mental health awareness as Danny tells his story in a unique way, as he learns to come to terms with the barbaric and vicious murder of his best mate. Although, of course, he never does come to terms with such a cruel act. You can’t. \n\nSometimes Danny is, to use his own words, all lopsided in his head, which is why I’ve chosen to present the book in the current format, to expose how his thinking bounces around without rhyme or reason. So he discusses anxiety and depression and suicide and then out of the blue he writes a poem, but poetry is Danny’s way of clearing his head.\n\nWhat can I tell you about Danny? He has a ferocious spirit and vigour. He has high moods and an instinctive ability to perceive and understand the world around him. He has a fierce sense of loyalty, he’s romantic, quixotic and starry-eyed. He brings smiles to everyone he meets, a gift I truly believe comes from a higher source. \n\nHowever, there’s no denying that at times he can be restless, carrying the capacity for vastly darker moods, melancholy energies and occasional bouts of madness. \n\nWriters, poets, artists, musicians and circus clowns often suffer from boisterous and raucous dispositions. And it’s true they can get into trouble at times. They wear their moods as their ships of passage, and Danny is no different. He suffers from what Lord Byron would term a ‘fine madness.’ \n\nHe throws out poems in a sparkle of energy. And he puts everything into the words. They just arrive on paper as though a higher being is working through him. I can’t explain this, but it’s how it happens\n\nI’ve known Danny for over 40 years, since we shared a room together at a seaside town in the South coast of England. So my opinion? He’s probably a bit of a mad genius, slowly losing his sanity, although he loves the world and everyone in it, and if this book can help just one person then Danny will sleep with a smile on his face tonight. \n\nKarl Wiggins<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2283269805371540818\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4596365226761969357">J M (Jackie) Johnson is a freelance writer and e-book author based in the United Kingdom (Britain). She has published three books in the Starbirth science fiction and fantasy series:<br/><br/>Starbirth Assignment Shifter (updated 2019)<br/>The Shifter Dimension (updated 2019)<br/>Shadow Team GB (2015, updated 2018)<br/>She has finished the fourth and final book in the Starbirth series, Shadow Unleashed, and it will be pub</span>
  <span id="freeText4596365226761969357" style="display:none">J M (Jackie) Johnson is a freelance writer and e-book author based in the United Kingdom (Britain). She has published three books in the Starbirth science fiction and fantasy series:<br /><br />Starbirth Assignment Shifter (updated 2019)<br />The Shifter Dimension (updated 2019)<br />Shadow Team GB (2015, updated 2018)<br />She has finished the fourth and final book in the Starbirth series, Shadow Unleashed, and it will be published in 2019. She is a member of several online writing groups.<br /><br />J M previously worked in a professional capacity as a podiatrist in the National Health Service but always had a desire to be an author.<br /><br />She belonged to a spiritual group for eight years, following a particular spiritual lifestyle and making three pilgrimage trips to India. Her involvement fostered a lifelong fascination with powers of the mind. Two decades later she had the opportunity to join a group run by British ex-Special Forces and was a civilian member for six years. During that time she did extensive research into the military and intelligence worlds. These background experiences helped in the creation of her books.</span>

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
